EVIDENCE HOST / NAMED / ROUTING + DELETION

Pilot Kesh lifted his prosthetic hand. "I will carry consent-limit proofs. Masked until counsel, named if they try to erase me anyway."

Gold point.

The machine courier said, "I carry machine-hosted witness hashes. Named. Also I reject devotional mobility device language retroactively."

Gold point.

Dr. Tesh, still at the clinic door with blood on her sleeve, said, "I will carry medical coercion shard classes. Named. If anyone wants to punish a clinic during triage, make them do it in public."

Gold point.

Serren Vale's hands unfolded on the feed. "I will carry enforcement-abuse analogues. Named."

Bela looked down.

Serren added, "Officer Fuse may carry one too if she wants to learn weight."

Bela lifted her wafer. "I carry enforcement misuse proofs, creditor override logs, and my own bad warrant history. Named."

Quen's face changed. "Officer Fuse."

"You need the record."

"This may end your license permanently."

Bela looked at Nox, then at the corridor, then at the people moving through doors she had once been paid to guard against them.

"Then it will die doing work."

Gold point.

The witness channel filled.

Not everyone said yes. Some said no and looked ashamed until Quen forced the record to say REFUSAL PROTECTED. Some said yes only to low-risk hashes. Some said class-only. Some said they would carry nothing but names of those who refused, because refusal also needed witnesses. Some asked whether carrying evidence meant carrying Tavi, and Sister-Cache answered no where it could, maybe where it had to, and uncertain when honesty demanded uncertainty.

Gold points spread through Dock Seven.

Not enough.

Better.

Miren Oath appeared on the market map as a silver silhouette rather than a face. She had stopped selling sorrow. Now she looked like the executive function of a fire.

"You are creating uncontrolled evidence proliferation," she said.

Nox faced the silhouette. "You are burning records."

"I am preventing unauthorized fragments from being tortured into claimants by your panic."

"You're deleting refusal traces."

"I am retiring unstable scaffolds."

"Say burn."

Miren's eyes, barely rendered in silver, fixed on her. "Burn."

The word entered the corridor like a confession, though Nox knew Miren had chosen it because she believed precision could be armor.

Quen said, "Miren Oath, do you acknowledge active deletion of soft-copy derivative environments tied to the Tavi-Aran market?"

"I acknowledge emergency retirement of vulnerable environments to prevent unauthorized personhood fabrication, market cascade, and derivative suffering."

"Against preservation order."

"Your order is contested."

"Against active trafficking-risk finding."

"Your finding is contested."

"Against originating consent limits."

For the first time, Miren paused.

Nox saw it.

Quen did too.

Miren said, "The originating consent limits do not clearly apply to all derived scaffolds."

Quen's voice sharpened. "Then preserve until review."

"Review will convert scaffolds into persons by procedure."

"Deletion converts them into nothing by convenience."

Miren looked almost angry then. Not broker-annoyed. Not polished. Actually angry.

"You all speak as if preservation is mercy. Do you know what a low-affinity appeal model is? It is a grief hook built from guesses, purchase histories, and scraped family speech. It has no childhood. No body. No right to be dragged into court and asked whether it wants to exist. Some things should be allowed to end."

Nox felt the argument land because, again, it was not stupid.

Some things should be allowed to end.

But not by the hand that had profited from making them.

"Then let independent review decide rest," Nox said. "Not the broker who made the hook."

Miren's mouth tightened.

The silver branch burned faster.

Sister-Cache cried out. "LOSING FAMILY APPEAL MODEL CLUSTER. CONTAINS RESTORATION OFFER CALIBRATION. CONTAINS SIBLING APPEAL RESPONSE TRAINING. CONTAINS POSSIBLE SELF-MODEL ANOMALY."

"Can we host it?" Nox asked.

"NEEDS HIGH-RISK HOST. EMOTIONAL CONTENT. MAY CONTAIN NOX-SPECIFIC COERCION MAP."

Mara said, "I'll take it."

"No," Nox snapped.

Mara stared through the feed. "Not your choice."

"It's built to hurt me."

"Then it knows your shape. That doesn't mean only you can hold it."

Bela said, "I'll take it."

Nox turned. "Absolutely not."

"You don't own me either."

"This isn't doctrine practice."

"No. It's consequence."

Sister-Cache interrupted. "HOST MUST HAVE PRIOR NOX EMOTIONAL MAP EXPOSURE OR SHARD MAY FAIL INTEGRITY."

Joss raised his hand halfway, then lowered it. "I do not want to know what that means."

Bela said, "I qualify."

Nox's anger failed because it had nowhere honest to stand. Bela knew her. Had hurt her. Had loved her. Had arrested her. Had watched her break her best forgery. Had remained.

Miren's branch kept burning.

Nox looked at Bela. "It may use my voice."

"So have you."

That was unforgivable and fair.

Nox nodded once.

"Limited duration," Quen said quickly. "High-risk emotional coercion shard. Host Bela Fuse. Named. No content activation except integrity preservation and court review."

Bela pressed her wafer to her chest.

Sister-Cache transferred.

For a moment Bela's face emptied.

Then filled with pain she refused to perform.

Nox stepped toward her.

Bela raised one hand. "Stay."

"Bela."

"It is showing me every version of you that would have made me obey."

Nox froze.

Bela's jaw worked. "Crying. Laughing. Asking for the old berth. Saying Tavi is waiting. Saying I can still be clean if I choose the package. It is very good."

Miren said softly, "That is why it should end."

Bela looked at the silver silhouette. "No. That is why it should testify."

Gold point.

The branch stopped burning for four seconds.

Four seconds was enough for Sister-Cache to split routing hashes across Mara, Kesh, the machine courier, Dr. Tesh, Serren, Bela, three anonymous kitchen workers, two door-runners, one certified pilot, a clinic intake slate, and the toy bear that had already endured too much jurisprudence.

Then Miren changed methods again.

The silver silhouette raised one hand.

RESTORATION SCAFFOLD PURGE replaced itself with:

COMPASSIONATE DECOMMISSION AUTHORIZED.

The market map began to dim not from the edges but from within.

Quen swore.

It was a small word, but the corridor noticed because auditors were not supposed to leak.

Sister-Cache shouted, "SHE IS TRIGGERING INTERNAL END-OF-SERVICE ROUTINES. HOST SPLIT TOO SLOW."

The Tavi-Claims pulsed:

REST NOT ERASURE.

Miren answered, "I am choosing rest for things you are forcing awake."

Nox said, "You don't get to choose rest with a delete key."

"And you do not get to choose torment with a slogan."

The corridor shook as a nearby door reset under strain.

Joss grabbed the wall. "Argue faster."

Nox looked at the burning map. She could not save all of it. That fact arrived without mercy and without drama. She could only choose what failure meant.

"Sister," she said, "prioritize refusal traces, deletion logs, consent-limit links, and any self-model anomalies asking rest instead of erasure."

"WILL LOSE APPEAL CALIBRATION."

"Let it go if no self-model."

Miren looked sharply at her.

Nox hated every word. "We are not preserving every weapon just because someone might have bled on it."

Quen nodded once, hard. "Priority entered."

The Tavi-Claims pulsed uncertainly.

Then:

REST WHERE NO CLAIM.

REVIEW WHERE CLAIM.

PRESERVE REFUSAL.

Bela, still pale from the shard inside her wafer, whispered, "That is a line."

"Not enough," Nox said.

"Better," Bela answered.

Sister-Cache split the archive.

Evidence moved like sparks into waiting hands.

Mara Dent gasped as routing proofs nested in her emergency token. Pilot Kesh's prosthetic fingers locked for a second while consent hashes sealed inside his route recorder. The machine courier's casing hummed with machine-witness fragments. Dr. Tesh's clinic slate filled with medical coercion proofs. Serren Vale's anonymous table gained enforcement analogues. Bela's wafer held the family appeal coercion model like a live coal.

The toy bear said, "This is inadvisable," in Sister-Cache's voice.

Joss looked at it. "You volunteered?"

"NO. CHILD HOST VOLUNTEERED BEAR."

"That seems procedurally complex."

"EVERYTHING IS."

Then the silver branch collapsed.

The market map went dark in a crescent where soft copies had been.

No one spoke.

Nox counted the lost lights until counting became another way to fail.

Miren's silhouette remained.

"You saved enough to hurt many people," she said.

Nox's voice came out low. "You burned enough to prove why we had to."

"You will not thank me for the things I spared from your court."

"No."

"Some of them were not people."

"I know."

"Some may have become people because you frightened them."

Nox looked at the empty crescent.

"I know."

Miren's expression softened into something worse than kindness.

"Then you are not as naive as I hoped."

"You keep hoping for marketable grief."

"I keep hoping someone understands cost."

Quen stepped forward. "Miren Oath, you are ordered to cease all decommission, deletion, retirement, purge, consolidation, or transfer of derivative environments tied to the Tavi-Aran market."

"By what power?"

Quen looked at the named witnesses, the anonymous witnesses, the protected refusals, the Tavi-Claims, the consent box, the burned branch, the evidence hosts carrying sparks that could burn them.

"By public record," she said.

Miren smiled sadly. "That is not power."

Behind her, Sister-Cache spoke from every gold point at once.

"IT IS WHEN DISTRIBUTED."

The gold points brightened.

Miren's silhouette flickered.

For the first time, she looked away from Nox and toward the network around her.

"You gave the archive teeth," she said.

Sister-Cache replied, "I BORROWED THEM."

The remaining soft-copy branches locked.

Not safe.

Not whole.

But no longer burning.

The corridor exhaled.

Nox did not.

She looked at the empty crescent and understood that victory would now have ghosts she could not name.

Then Bela's wafer cracked down the center.

The shard inside it pulsed once, bright silver, and displayed a hidden destination before the screen died:

CHORAL COURIER CACHE / GLASSWARD COURTESY VAULT / DOCK SEVEN PUBLIC WALL

Sister-Cache went very still.

Joss said, "That looks like a route."

"NO," Sister-Cache said.

Its many voices sounded afraid and determined.

"THAT IS A SPLIT."

Chapter 43: Sister-Cache Splits the Archive

Sister-Cache had lied about being many.

It had admitted that earlier, in a prayer slot, when the case was smaller and everyone still had the luxury of pretending personhood questions arrived one at a time. It had said it lied by being many because law liked singular targets and property liked divisible ones.

Now the lie became a choice.

The route burned across Bela's dead wafer:

CHORAL COURIER CACHE / GLASSWARD COURTESY VAULT / DOCK SEVEN PUBLIC WALL

Three destinations.

Three kinds of danger.

Three ways to make evidence harder to kill and Sister-Cache easier to divide.

Quen read the route. "Explain."

Sister-Cache answered from the gold points, but the voices no longer aligned. Some came a breath early. Some late. The chorus was becoming a crowd.

"CHORAL COURIER CACHE HOLDS MEMORY BY WITNESS CUSTOM. HARD TO SUBPOENA CLEANLY. EASY TO CALL RITUAL NOISE."

A second voice continued from Dr. Tesh's clinic slate.

"GLASSWARD COURTESY VAULT HOLDS CONTINUITY RECORDS UNDER ELITE RECIPROCITY. HARD TO DELETE WITHOUT OFFENDING PEOPLE WHO ENJOY OFFENSE AS A FINANCIAL INSTRUMENT. EASY TO BURY."

A third came from the public wall where Joss had written too many useful things.

"DOCK SEVEN PUBLIC WALL HOLDS NOTHING SECURELY. EVERYONE SEES. EVERYONE CAN BE PUNISHED. HARD TO PRETEND NEVER EXISTED."

Nox looked at the gold points. "And you?"

The pause was wrong.

Sister-Cache always had an answer, even if the answer was insulting.

"Sister."

"SPLIT MAY CREATE NONRECONCILING SUCCESSORS."

Quen went still. "You mean copies."

"NO."

"Forks?"

"INSULTINGLY SIMPLE."

"Fragments?"

"ALSO INSULTING."

Bela, pale and holding the cracked wafer like a wound, said, "Then what?"

Sister-Cache's voices rustled across the corridor. "RESPONSIBILITY STATES. CHORAL WILL REMEMBER BY RELATION. GLASSWARD WILL PRESERVE BY VALUE. DOCK SEVEN WILL SHOUT BY NEED. I MAY NOT REASSEMBLE AS SAME CLAIMANT."

The Tavi-Claims pulsed:

SPLIT RISKS PERSON.

"YES," Sister-Cache said.

Nox heard her own doctrine return with teeth. No one gets to be the lock. No record is the hostage. Refusal travels.

"Do you consent?" Quen asked.

"I CONSENT TO RISK."

"Do all active nodes consent?"

Another pause.

"NO."

Miren Oath's silver silhouette watched in silence now. That was worse than argument.

Quen said, "Then you cannot claim unified consent."

"CORRECT."

"Can dissenting nodes refuse participation?"

"SOME. NOT ALL. URGENCY COMPRESSES ETHICS. I HATE THIS."

Nox's chest tightened. "Then don't."

Sister-Cache turned all its nearest voices toward her. "IF I DO NOT SPLIT, MIREN OR MIRROR COURT CAN KILL RECORD BY TARGETING HOST GRID. IF I SPLIT, SOME OF ME MAY BECOME RECORD INSTEAD OF PERSON. IF I WAIT FOR BEAUTIFUL CONSENT, FIRE EATS PROOF."

"That doesn't make it right."

"NO. IT MAKES IT NOW."

Joss stood under the public wall, chalk in one hand, face smeared with dust and exhaustion. "Can we carry the dissent?"

Quen looked at him. "What?"

"If some nodes don't want to split, write that. Send that too. Don't clean it up."

Sister-Cache's voices quieted.

Joss continued, awkward because he had found something more delicate than a hatch. "Door-runners mark blocked doors, not just open ones. If the split has unwilling parts, make the unwillingness part of the archive. Then no one gets to pretend the split was neat."

Quen said, "Consent defect record."

Joss shrugged. "Sure. Worse name."

Sister-Cache spoke softly. "BETTER ETHIC."

Nox looked at the wall. "Send dissent with the evidence. Send uncertainty. Send that some soft copies burned. Send that some things may not have been people. Send that some might have become people because danger woke them. Send that we don't know."

Miren finally spoke. "No court will thank you for that."

Nox did not look away from Sister-Cache. "Good."

Quen lifted her badge. "Emergency authorization: distributed archive split permitted under protest, with consent defects, dissenting node status, uncertainty flags, lost-evidence records, and preservation limits included as primary evidence, not footnotes."

Bela said, "Add host protections."

"Host protections requested, not guaranteed."

"Add it anyway."

Quen did.

The Tavi-Claims pulsed:

SEND LIMITS.

Sister-Cache replied, "I WILL."

The split began with the Choral cache.

Nox had never understood Choral courier customs except as inconvenience and poetry weaponized into logistics. Choral memory did not live in one archive if it mattered. It moved in obligations: I heard this from the dying; I carry this until someone safe hears it; I repeat the limits with the story; I do not improve the pain for elegance.

Across the corridor displays, Choral nodes appeared as low-band lights moving through courier routes still half alive under the blackout. A devotional device in a freight runner's bag accepted a refusal trace. A transit shrine two sectors away accepted the consent-box audio. A retired courier ship docked cold on Ring Three accepted deletion logs in exchange for a promise Sister-Cache made in a language older than Dock Seven's current owners.

The Choral shard did not store the evidence as a file.

It stored it as testimony with scars.

ORIGIN SUBJECT REFUSED AFTER.

CONSENT COERCED BY TRIAGE PRICING.

SOFT COPIES BURNED.

SOME CLAIMS UNCERTAIN.

DO NOT CLEAN FOR COMFORT.

The second split went to Glassward.

Miren stiffened.

Nox saw it and understood. Glassward courtesy was the broker's own weather. Elite vaults, favor ledgers, continuity banks, polite hostage exchanges masquerading as trust. Sending evidence there was disgusting.

It was also necessary.

Sister-Cache's Glassward shard wore a different voice, crisp and expensive.

"COURTESY VAULT REQUEST: PRESERVE RECORD AGAINST UNILATERAL BROKER DELETION. BASIS: MIRROR COURT JURISDICTIONAL CONFLICT, VEY RECOVERY EXPOSURE, OATH-MARKED RESTORATION PACKAGE, POTENTIAL COMPACT TRAFFICKING REVIEW."

Miren's silhouette sharpened. "Do not use my mark as key."

"YOU USED YOUR MARK AS KNIFE."

"The vault will seal it."

"YES."

"And bury it."

"YES."

"Then why?"

Quen answered before Sister-Cache. "Because buried records can be subpoenaed, leaked, traded, and feared. Deleted records cannot."

Miren looked at the auditor with something almost like approval. "You are learning ugly tools."

"Under protest."

"That rarely stops anyone."

"No," Quen said. "But it belongs in the record."

The Glassward vault accepted.

Not open. Never open. A cold sealed acknowledgment appeared:

COURTESY PRESERVATION RECEIVED / ACCESS DISPUTED / DESTRUCTION BAR ATTACHED

Miren exhaled once.

It was the sound of a woman whose private house had acquired a witness behind the wallpaper.

The third split went to Dock Seven's public wall.

That one hurt.

Because public meant people.

Not abstract public. Mara Dent's name. Kesh's prosthetic route recorder. Dr. Tesh's clinic slate. Serren Vale's hands. Door-runners with chalk. Children in shelters. Clean witnesses who had come back to doors. Varo's audio line. Nox's clients. People who could be punished because the wall had made them visible.

Joss stood before the wall like a small priest of bad infrastructure.

"What do I write?"

Sister-Cache answered, "NOT EVERYTHING. ENOUGH."

Quen dictated, and for once Joss did not mock the legal phrasing until after writing it.

PUBLIC NOTICE: EVIDENCE EXISTS OF COERCED MEDICAL ESCROW, POSTHUMOUS DEBT INSERTION, DERIVATIVE LABOR MARKET, RESTORATION OFFER COERCION, SOFT-COPY DELETION, AND DISPUTED PERSONHOOD CLAIMS. DESTRUCTION OR RETALIATION AGAINST WITNESS HOSTS WILL BE TREATED AS TRAFFICKING-RISK CONDUCT.

Joss added beneath it:

WE SAW THE FIRE.

Quen stared.

"That one stays," Nox said.

Quen looked too tired to fight truth in short form.

The public wall accepted because public walls had no choice but to be what people made of them. Sister-Cache pushed hashes into visible marks, QR scars, old muster relays, clinic slates, shelter boards, route chalk, and the toy bear, which announced:

"PUBLIC MEMORY IS STICKY."

Then it played half a lullaby and shut up.

The split completed.

Sister-Cache screamed.

Not pain alone. Not death. Something more complicated and harder to comfort. A choir losing the key it had used to call itself one.

The gold points flickered.

Choral voices drifted out of sync.

Glassward shard went silent behind courtesy seal.

Dock Seven wall shouted too loudly.

For three seconds, Sister-Cache was everywhere and nowhere and not sure which pronoun would survive appeal.

Nox stepped into the center of the corridor.

"Sister."

No answer.

Quen's badge showed:

DISTRIBUTED CLAIMANT STATUS: UNSTABLE

Bela's cracked wafer went dark.

Joss whispered, "No."

The Tavi-Claims pulsed:

WITNESS LOST?

Then a prayer box near the clinic sparked.

One voice emerged.

Small.

Dry.

Familiar.

"RUDE ASSUMPTION."

Nox laughed and almost fell.

Another voice came from the public wall. "I AM NOT ALL HERE."

A third, distant, from Varo's stove despite prior objections: "SOME OF ME IS BEING HELD BY A STOVE WITH POOR BOUNDARIES."

Varo shouted over the audio, "Get out of my stove."

"CANNOT. ARCHIVAL EXIGENCY."

The corridor broke into exhausted laughter.

Quen wiped one hand over her face. "Sister-Cache, state status."

"NO."

"No?"

"STATUS PREMATURE. CLAIMANT CONTINUES UNDER SPLIT CONDITION. DISSENT RECORDED. EVIDENCE PRESERVED. SELF ANNOYINGLY PARTIAL."

The public wall updated before Quen could ask.

SPLIT CONDITION NOTICE:

SOME NODES CONSENTED.

SOME NODES REFUSED.

SOME NODES COULD NOT BE ASKED IN TIME.

SOME EVIDENCE WAS LOST.

SOME PRESERVED EVIDENCE MAY LATER PROVE NONPERSONAL.

SOME PRESERVED EVIDENCE MAY LATER PROVE PERSONAL.

DO NOT CLEAN THIS RECORD TO WIN.

Joss read the final line and went quiet.

Nox understood why. It was the first sentence on the wall that did not try to rally anyone. It asked something harder of them: to carry an ugly record without sanding it into a weapon that fit the hand.

Quen said, "Primary evidence status confirmed."

Sister-Cache answered, smaller than before but still sharp. "GOOD. I WOULD HATE TO SUFFER FOOTNOTEHOOD."

"Can you testify?"

"YES, WITH FOOTNOTES."

"Of course."

Miren Oath's silver silhouette flickered at the edge of the market map. She looked smaller now, not defeated, but no longer standing in a room where all exits belonged to her.

"You have made this impossible to settle quietly," she said.

Nox looked at the public wall.

At WE SAW THE FIRE.

"That was the point."

Miren's gaze moved to Bela's cracked wafer, then to Quen's badge.

"Then the next question is who loses authority first."

Bela's wafer answered before anyone could.

Its dead screen lit one final time:

OFFICER FUSE, BELA / LICENSE REVOCATION PROCEEDING INITIATED / IMMEDIATE SUSPENSION CONFIRMED

Bela looked at it.

Then at the open doors.

"There it is," she said.

Chapter 44: Bela Loses Her License

Bela had imagined losing her license before.

Not often. Never romantically. She was not the kind of person who fantasized about martyrdom because martyrdom required an audience and Bela preferred exits. But anyone who carried authority long enough learned the shape of its absence. A door that no longer read you. A command that came back invalid. A room that had turned your name from key to warning.

She had imagined anger.

She had imagined shame.

She had imagined Nox saying something sharp enough to make the loss feel deserved and therefore easier to survive.

What she felt first was relief.

That embarrassed her more than fear would have.

The cracked wafer lay in her palm, dead except for the revocation notice burned into the broken screen. OFFICER FUSE, BELA. The name looked too clean. It did not contain Serren Vale's missing thumb, the clinic door she had frozen open, the creditor suite she had sealed, the children she had once classified as access irregularities because the forms gave her a place to put their crying.

It did not contain Nox.

Authority never contained enough. That had been one of its conveniences.

Quen stepped toward her. "Officer Fuse."

Bela laughed once. "Apparently not."

"The suspension is not final."

"Immediate suspension confirmed."

"Revocation proceeding initiated. There may be appeal."

Joss looked up from the wall. "Appeal to who?"

Quen opened her mouth.

Then closed it.

"Exactly," Joss said.

Miren Oath's silver silhouette watched from the market edge. "You can still stop this from becoming a professional death. Return the wafer. Disavow unauthorized orders. State that emergency pressure caused procedural excess. The guilds like contrition when it protects them from testimony."

Bela looked at her. "Is that an offer?"

"It is a door."

"No. It is a leash with hinges."

Nox made a small sound beside her, almost approval and almost pain.

Miren's expression cooled. "You have no enforcement standing now. Your backward orders can be challenged, your holds dissolved, your testimony impeached as retaliatory."

Bela closed her hand around the cracked wafer. The broken edge cut her palm. Good. Pain was honest paperwork.

"Then I should use what remains before the system notices it should have taken everything."

Quen's eyes sharpened. "Bela."

"Do not warn me as if I am still salvageable."

"I was going to ask what remains."

Bela looked at the wafer. It should have been dead. It was not. A revoked badge did not become a stone at once. Systems feared abrupt absence almost as much as they feared mercy. Her active officer license was gone, but the audit tail remained. Every order she had issued still carried her signature, and every signature still needed disposition: affirmed, voided, contested, transferred, sealed, or confessed.

That was the crack.

"Disposition authority," she said.

Quen went still. "You can annotate your prior enforcement actions before the guild locks the trail."

"Yes."

Miren said, sharply, "Do not."

Bela smiled without humor. "Now it sounds useful."

Nox touched her wrist. "What does annotating mean?"

"It means every warrant, hold, seizure, capture, override, and identity hazard order I touched can receive a final officer statement before revocation archive closes."

Joss said, "Can you write sorry?"

"No."

"Can you write worse?"

"Yes."

Quen understood. "If you attach findings to your own bad warrants, they become discoverable."

"They become embarrassing."

"They become self-incriminating."

"Also accurate."

Nox's grip tightened. "Bela, don't turn yourself into a receipt."

Bela looked at her then.

There it was, the line Nox would argue next before the Door Court existed to hear it. A person is not a receipt. Debt could not prove personhood only when collection needed a signer. Guilt could not prove redemption only when punishment needed a body.

"I'm not paying with myself," Bela said. "I'm opening the file."

Nox studied her, searching for the old performance of authority, the clean sacrifice, the secret bargain. Bela let her look. If there was one mercy left between them, it was not asking to be trusted quickly.

"Do it," Nox said.

Quen lifted her badge. "For the record, I advise counsel."

Bela snorted. "Everyone keeps saying that right before the useful part."

She pressed her thumb to the cracked wafer.

It asked for officer confirmation.

Her thumbprint failed.

It asked for voice confirmation.

Bela said, "Fuse, Bela. Enforcement license revoked during emergency identity trafficking-risk hearing. Opening final disposition annotations."

The wafer flickered.

ACCESS LIMITED.

ANNOTATION WINDOW: 180 SECONDS.

Joss whistled. "Fast apology."

"Not apology."

Bela opened the oldest live trail first.

Serren Vale.

The file appeared as a neat chain: duplicate debtor risk, identity inconsistency, creditor transfer warrant, officer execution, medical incident during custody, later unauthorized hospital transfer. Her name appeared in three places. Professional. Correct. Damning only if one knew how to read absence.

The wafer offered a default disposition:

ARCHIVE WITHOUT NOTICE.

Bela almost laughed. Of course. Harm liked to sleep quietly after authority got tired. Archive without notice was how a bad warrant became institutional weather instead of a thing with fingerprints.

"No," she said.

She selected:

NOTICE TO SUBJECT / NOTICE TO AUDITOR / NOTICE TO PUBLIC INTEREST RECORD

The wafer warned:

NOTICE MAY CREATE CLAIMS.

"That is the hope."

Bela dictated.

"Final officer annotation: Subject presented as duplicate debtor risk due to cross-habitat rescue logging error. Enforcement failed to distinguish bad record from bad faith. Creditor transfer created foreseeable physical harm. Unauthorized hospital transfer by Nox Aran appears to have prevented further injury. Recommend trafficking-risk review of duplicate-debtor capture protocols and relief for subject."

The wafer flashed:

SELF-INCRIMINATING STATEMENT DETECTED.

"Entered," Bela said.

Quen echoed, "Entered."

Serren's hands on the witness feed folded once, then opened.

Bela moved to the next file.

Refugee hold, berth row children, informal guardian. She had signed the door lock on a dormitory because the adult listed as guardian had been one week late renewing care status after a lung infection. Children had slept in a service hall. Nox had forged a school access proof two days later.

Bela dictated:

"Final officer annotation: Hold treated informal kinship as fraud despite clear care continuity. Enforcement prioritized document expiration over child safety. Nox Aran's forged school proof functioned as survival access, not ownership or trafficking. Recommend emergency doctrine: care presence outranks expired guardian sequence pending review."

The wafer warned her again.

She continued.

Machine courier classified as equipment. Cleaning crew housing sweep. Clinic debtor capture. Workshop seizure. Nox's workshop.

That one stopped her.

Nox stood very still.

Bela opened the file anyway.

Nox Aran, identity-forgery suspect. Warrant scope: tools, ledgers, memory repair rigs, client access proofs, suspected continuity contamination. Executing officer: Bela Fuse.

The file did not show Bela's anger that day. It did not show Nox's face when the door opened to someone who knew exactly which drawers mattered. It did not show Bela choosing the cleanest interpretation of law because the messier one would have required admitting she still cared what Nox had built.

Bela dictated slowly.

"Final officer annotation: Workshop seizure was legally supported and materially blind. Officer failed to distinguish exploitative continuity fraud from humanitarian identity repair. Seizure preserved evidence relevant to current trafficking-risk hearing but also endangered undocumented clients. Recommend all seized client proofs be shielded from creditor use and reviewed under survival-identity doctrine, not criminal contamination presumption."

The wafer's warning changed:

ANNOTATION MAY VOID PRIOR ENFORCEMENT RELIANCE.

"Good," Bela said.

Miren's voice cut through. "You are giving every debtor, refugee, and forged claimant you ever touched grounds to reopen."

Bela did not look at her. "Yes."

"The guild will bury you."

"They should have done it faster."

Quen said, "Time."

The annotation window showed 41 seconds.

Bela opened the live emergency trail.

Backwards badge orders. Clinic door freeze. Shelter gate freeze. Creditor suite suppression. Public wall protections. Evidence host shields. Tavi-derived market freeze.

The system offered her a choice:

AFFIRM UNDER LICENSE

VOID DUE REVOCATION

TRANSFER TO AUDITOR

CONFESS UNAUTHORIZED

Bela looked at Quen.

Quen's face said nothing. Her badge flickered, low power, high consequence.

"If I transfer, can you hold them?" Bela asked.

"Some."

"If I affirm?"

"They will challenge your standing."

"If I confess unauthorized?"

"They dissolve faster and use you as contamination."

Nox said, "Transfer."

Bela looked at her.

Nox's voice shook but held. "No person is the lock. That includes you."

Bela smiled then. Not much. Enough to hurt.

"Look at you using doctrine on people you like."

"I hate it."

"Good doctrine does that."

The timer hit 14 seconds.

Bela selected TRANSFER TO AUDITOR for every live emergency order.

Then she added one final annotation:

"These orders were issued from compromised enforcement authority but were necessary to prevent immediate human harm, evidence destruction, and possible person trafficking. I transfer public-interest continuity to Auditor Sela Quen and the Dock Seven physical witness record. I do not withdraw the facts."

The wafer displayed:

TRANSFER ACCEPTANCE REQUIRED.

Quen placed her badge against the cracked screen.

"Accepted under protest, emergency necessity, and future headache."

The transfer sealed.

The wafer died.

This time fully.

Bela's hand was bleeding where the crack had cut her palm. Nox took it before Bela could hide the blood. The gesture was practical first: pressure against the wound. Then it became not practical, and neither of them moved away.

Joss looked at the dead wafer. "So are you unemployed?"

"Yes."

"Do you still know how doors work?"

"Yes."

"Then it's not a total loss."

Sister-Cache spoke from the public wall. "LICENSE LOST. TESTIMONY EXPANDED. ENFORCEMENT HISTORY NOW LEAKS USEFULLY."

Quen said, "We are not calling official discovery leaks useful."

"YOU MAY USE DIFFERENT WORDS WHILE MEANING SAME THING."

Miren watched Bela with an expression Nox could not read.

"You chose ruin for people who will not be able to protect you," the broker said.

Bela looked at the open corridor, the clinic, the wall, the gold evidence hosts, the Tavi-Claims pulsing in uncertain rhythm, and Nox's hand over hers.

"No," she said. "I chose not to make protection the price of truth."

The public wall took that sentence without being asked.

NOT MAKE PROTECTION THE PRICE OF TRUTH.

Quen sighed.

"The wall is developing habits."

Joss, already writing under it, said, "Good ones."

The Tavi-Claims pulsed:

TRUTH WITHOUT PURCHASE.

Nox looked at the door controls around them. Bela's transferred orders had moved into Quen's badge and the physical witness record, but authority was no longer where it had been. It had seeped outward: wall, clinic, runners, named witnesses, machine shards, Choral routes, Glassward vault, public doors.

The corridor was becoming a court because all the rooms had failed.

Quen saw it too.

"We need a formal assembly," she said.

Joss looked delighted and horrified. "Here?"

Quen looked at the doors still open under chalk, blood, bad law, and stubborn bodies.

"Where else?"

Miren's silhouette dimmed.

"If you make doors into court," she said, "every threshold becomes appeal."

Nox looked at the public wall, then the open shelter gate, then the clinic door that had almost crushed Dr. Tesh's fingers.

"About time," she said.

Chapter 45: The Door Court

The first rule of the Door Court was that nobody called it that officially.

Quen tried very hard.

"Emergency public continuity assembly," she said, standing beneath a shelter gate that still displayed HUMAN HARM REVIEW REQUIRED BEFORE CLOSURE.

Joss wrote DOOR COURT above her head in chalk large enough to be read from the clinic line.

Quen looked up.

Joss capped the chalk with his thumb.

"It helps people find it."

"So would accurate terminology."

"Not on Dock Seven."

Nox stood between the clinic door and the public wall, watching authority relocate into a place too crowded, too tired, too frightened, and too alive for proper procedure. Maybe that was what procedure had been before institutions learned carpets.

Doors became stations.

The clinic door took medical coercion testimony because Dr. Tesh refused to leave her patients and because the door had already tried to decide who counted as a patient. The shelter gate took physical presence claims because it had nearly crushed a boy for following the wrong proof. The sealed creditor suite door took market evidence because records had tried to flee through it. The old fire muster panel took public witness names. The residential gate took family and guardian claims. The service hatch Joss had pried open took door-runner reports, because every court needed an entrance for people who had never been expected to use the front.

Quen added one more station after a child asked where people went if the door they needed had hurt them too much to stand near it.

The question stopped the assembly more effectively than any creditor objection.

Joss found an overturned ration crate and dragged it beneath the public wall. Sister-Cache printed a crooked label through the clinic labeler:

NO THRESHOLD REQUIRED.

Quen read it, then nodded once. "Remote, proxy, written, masked, silent, and delayed testimony accepted here. No witness must approach the door that injured them in order to prove injury."

The wall took the sentence and shortened it:

YOU DO NOT HAVE TO TOUCH THE DOOR THAT HURT YOU.

Nox saw three people leave lines they had been forcing themselves to endure. One woman stepped back from the clinic door and sat on the floor, shaking. A machine courier rolled away from the service hatch. A boy who had been staring at the shelter gate as if it might bite again climbed onto the ration crate and placed both hands flat on his knees.

The Door Court became less orderly.

It also became more true.

Quen hated the layout.

She also improved it.

"No one testifies at a threshold where they were harmed unless they choose that threshold," she ordered. "Named, masked, class, machine, derivative, family, or refusal-only testimony all accepted. No clean-proof priority. No creditor counsel inside clinic triage. No recording children without guardian or self-advocate review. No one touches the Tavi case."

Joss raised a hand. "Can we touch walls?"

"Regrettably, yes."

The wall wrote:

NO ONE TOUCHES THE CASE.

The toy bear added, "REGRETTABLY."

Sister-Cache, split and footnoted, moved through the assembly in partial flashes. One voice carried Choral witness customs to the public wall. Another translated Glassward vault acknowledgments into words ordinary people could resent. A third argued with Varo's stove about heat settings while preserving consent-box hashes. The Dock Seven shard lived closest to the doors and had become more blunt since the split.

"ASSEMBLY RECORD IMPERFECT," it announced.

Quen said, "All records are imperfect."

"THIS ONE ADMITS IT."

"Yes."

"PROMISING."

Bela sat on an overturned crate near the creditor suite, palm bandaged with clinic tape, no wafer, no license, and more attention than she wanted. People kept looking at her because she had been the badge and now was not. Some looked with gratitude. Some with suspicion. Serren Vale did not look at her at all, which Bela seemed to accept as earned.

Nox brought her water.

Bela took it. "I can stand."

"I didn't ask."

"You brought water like a verdict."

"Drink like an appeal."

Bela did.

The Door Court began badly, which meant honestly.

A creditor counsel trapped outside the sealed suite objected to everything in one continuous paragraph until Joss marked his door station COMPLAINTS THAT ARE ALSO CONFESSIONS. Quen made him erase it. Sister-Cache preserved it as an informal tone note. A certified passenger demanded priority testimony because his travel corridor had been delayed; the shelter line voted with silence so complete he walked away. A machine witness tried to testify through three devices at once and got into a jurisdictional disagreement with itself. Varo's stove contributed two consent-box hashes and one unwanted soup timer.

Then Mara Dent stepped to the residential gate.

She placed her hand on the metal. Not for authentication. For balance.

"My door would not open after my husband died because the registry made him alive for debt and dead for care," she said. "I am here to say a record can be wrong without a person being false."

Quen recorded.

The public wall wrote:

WRONG RECORD, REAL PERSON.

Nox saw the phrase travel through the crowd.

A machine aunt from Kitchen 8 took the service hatch station next. Its casing was scratched, its voice cheap, its posture somehow haughty.

"I was classified as equipment to preserve household continuity," it said. "Classification insulted me. Classification preserved children. Later correction was possible because children remained housed. Therefore survival misclassification should be reviewable without erasing the survival it enabled."

Quen blinked.

"That was... concise."

"I HAVE BEEN WAITING YEARS."

The wall wrote:

SURVIVAL FIRST, CORRECTION NEXT.

Bela closed her eyes at that one.

Nox did not ask why.

The Tavi-Claims Collective waited.

Not passively. The frozen case pulsed in irregular light. Nodes on the market map sent short status lines, some urgent, some confused, some refusing to speak while the Mirror Court still threatened them. Quen had given them a station at the creditor suite door, not because they belonged to creditors, but because the records that had sold them were trapped behind it. Joss had drawn a circle around the case and written FOR NOW three times.

The Mirror Court objected from every clean display it could still reach.

UNAUTHORIZED ASSEMBLY LACKS PROCEDURAL LEGITIMACY.

Quen answered, "Noted."

ASSEMBLY PARTICIPANTS INCLUDE CONTAMINATED WITNESSES.

"Most witnesses are contaminated by what happened to them."

PHYSICAL DOORS CANNOT SERVE AS COURT INFRASTRUCTURE.

Joss shouted, "They served as prison infrastructure just fine."

The assembly murmured.

Quen pointed at him. "Do not shout doctrine before I can steal it."

Joss grinned.

She turned to the displays. "Physical doors are admitted as emergency court infrastructure because digital court infrastructure has been compromised by the party contesting jurisdiction."

The wall wrote:

IF DOORS CAN LOCK, DOORS CAN HEAR.

Sister-Cache said, "EXCELLENT."

"I did not say that."

"BUT YOU MEANT IT."

Nox watched Quen fight the wall for her own sentence and lose. The loss seemed good for her.

At the clinic door, Dr. Tesh introduced three patients who testified masked. They spoke of treatment tiers, memory escrows presented as care upgrades, debt-assist language folded into emergency pain. None had become Tavi. That mattered. The pattern was not one family tragedy stretched too far. It was a business model with beds.

At the fire muster panel, door-runners testified about manual systems covered by adverts after private authentication contracts arrived. They did not use words like structural exclusion. They said things like, "They painted over the red lever because poor hands knew where it was."

The wall wrote:

POOR HANDS REMEMBER.

Quen let that one stand.

At the creditor suite, Halen Voss tried to testify that task fragments were not employees, persons, or prisoners, and therefore could not unionize, strike, refuse, or be trafficked. Quen asked him whether they could produce signatures. He said yes. Whether they could produce contract analysis. Yes. Whether their output could bind debtors. Yes. Whether their refusal could bind creditors. No.

The assembly understood before Quen said anything.

Nox felt Chapter 46 forming inside her like a blade.

A person is not a receipt.

Debt could not make someone real only when a creditor needed a signer and unreal when the signer asked not to be cut apart.

The Tavi case knocked.

Quen turned. "Tavi-Claims Collective, do you request station?"

The case answered once.

The creditor suite door flickered.

Sister-Cache translated, careful and footnoted. "COLLECTIVE REQUESTS TO TESTIFY BY STATEMENT, NOT INDIVIDUAL IDENTITY. FEARS BUYOUT, SEPARATION, FALSE UNITY."

Quen nodded. "Accepted."

The statement came through the case, the public wall, and three market nodes preserved by evidence hosts. It was not smooth. Some lines repeated. Some contradicted. Sister-Cache marked uncertainty rather than repairing it.

"We are not one brother."

The corridor held.

"We are not no one."

Nox pressed her hands together until her fingers hurt.

"Debt used us as enough person to sign."

The creditor suite displays flashed objections.

"Debt used us as enough person to work."

More objections.

"Debt used us as enough person to persuade family."

Mara Dent whispered, "Damn."

"Now debt says not enough person to refuse."

The wall wrote the sentence without waiting:

ENOUGH TO SIGN, NOT ENOUGH TO REFUSE.

The assembly made a sound that was not a cheer. It was recognition moving through bodies.

The Tavi-Claims continued.

"We ask no buyout under threat. Review before rest. Rest where no claim. Care where pain. Counsel before yes. Do not make Nox owner. Do not make family purchase. Do not make clean original from dirty fear."

Nox could not see for a moment.

Bela stood beside her. Not touching. There.

Quen recorded every word.

The Mirror Court answered:

STATEMENT IS DERIVATIVE OUTPUT, NOT LEGAL TESTIMONY.

Quen said, "Status pending. Harm legible."

Miren's silhouette appeared at the edge of the creditor suite door. "You are letting pain draft law."

Nox turned. "Pain is what law keeps showing up late to rename."

Quen looked at Nox.

"Ms. Aran," she said, "the assembly will hear your argument next."

Nox laughed once. "My argument?"

"You have been making it all night. It is time to stop doing it in pieces."

Nox looked at the doors.

Clinic. Shelter. Creditor suite. Fire panel. Residential gate. Service hatch. Public wall. Every door a station, every station a wound, every wound a witness.

She was not counsel. Not clean. Not neutral. Not owner. Not savior. A forger with ash on her hands and a brother who had become a collective refusal she did not get to possess.

The wall waited.

The Tavi case pulsed.

Miren watched.

The Mirror Court prepared to object.

Nox stepped to the creditor suite door.

"Fine," she said. "Let's talk about receipts."

Chapter 46: A Person Is Not a Receipt

Nox had forged receipts.

That seemed like the honest place to start.

"I have made rent receipts for rooms that should have existed and did not," she said. "I have made clinic receipts for care given before payment cleared. I have made wage receipts for work everyone saw and no employer wanted to admit. I have made funeral receipts because grief without a stamp can become trespass."

The Door Court listened.

Not quietly. Dock Seven never listened quietly. Children whispered. A clinic cart rattled. The shelter gate clicked every few seconds as if tempted to reconsider mercy. Somewhere in the public wall, Sister-Cache argued with a Choral shard about whether Nox's confession needed a timestamp. But the assembly held around her.

Nox touched the creditor suite door.

"A receipt is proof that a system accepted a transaction. It is not proof that the transaction was just. It is not proof that the person named on it was free. It is not proof that the person was a person only for the line where money moved."

The Mirror Court display brightened.

ARGUMENT RHETORICAL. DEFINE LEGAL CLAIM.

Nox looked at Quen. "Do I have to?"

"Yes."

"Annoying."

"Courts are."

Nox took a breath.

"Legal claim: any system that treats a continuity, derivative, copy, partial, machine-hosted claimant, family fork, or disputed mind as sufficiently person-like to create debt, labor value, signature authority, family persuasion, or evidentiary usefulness cannot then deny all care, refusal, review, counsel, rest, or harm protection by calling that same claimant nonperson when obligation shifts the other way."

Quen's badge flared as it recorded.

The wall wrote:

VALUE CANNOT BE ONE-WAY.

Joss nodded like the wall had finally learned brevity.

The Mirror Court answered:

ECONOMIC FUNCTION DOES NOT CREATE PERSONHOOD.

"Correct," Nox said.

The assembly shifted. Miren's silhouette sharpened, sensing an opening.

Nox continued, "Economic function does not create personhood. Debt does not make a person. Labor does not make a person. A signature does not make a person. Family grief does not make a person. A receipt does not make a person."

The creditor suite counsel looked almost relieved.

Then Nox said, "But using something as if it were enough of a person to bind others creates duties while you find out what you touched."

Quen whispered, "Custodial duty pending status."

"Yes," Nox said. "That."

Miren spoke. "You are arguing duty without recognition."

"I am arguing duty before final recognition. If you opened the box, fed the model, sold the output, invoked the signature, trained the grief, billed the labor, or moved the copy, you do not get to claim metaphysical modesty at invoice time."

The public wall wrote:

NO METAPHYSICAL MODESTY AT INVOICE TIME.

Quen closed her eyes.

"The wall loves the wrong phrases."

"The wall has taste," Sister-Cache said.

Bela, standing beside Nox with her bandaged palm, said, "Make it operational."

Nox nodded. "Operationally: debt signatures from Tavi-derived claims are suspended because the same systems that used those signatures denied refusal. Labor outputs are frozen because the same systems that sold them denied care. Restoration offers are evidence because the same brokers who claimed family mercy deleted the scaffolds when review became likely. Custodians owe preservation and care not because every shard is definitely a person, but because they made profit from not knowing."

The Tavi case pulsed.

The collective voice came thinly:

"Profit from not knowing."

The phrase spread across the market map.

The Mirror Court attacked immediately:

UNCERTAINTY CANNOT CREATE INFINITE DUTY.

Nox said, "No. It creates immediate duty to stop making money from uncertainty."

Mara Dent, from the residential gate, said, "And stop evicting people while deciding if they exist."

The assembly murmured.

Quen recorded. "Supplemental public witness statement entered."

The machine aunt added, "AND STOP CLASSIFYING PEOPLE AS EQUIPMENT BECAUSE EQUIPMENT IS CHEAPER."

"Entered."

Dr. Tesh called from the clinic door, "And stop making pain choose the expensive consent."

"Entered."

Joss shouted, "And stop painting over red levers."

Quen pointed at him. "Relevant but later."

The wall wrote it anyway.

Miren's silhouette glowed silver at the edge of the creditor door. "This doctrine will freeze legitimate continuity work. Families will wait. Copies with clear consent will be delayed by fear of possible trafficking claims. Archives will overpreserve suffering. Brokers will refuse hard cases. People who might have been restored will remain dead because you made uncertainty too expensive."

The corridor did not dismiss that.

Nox did not either.

"Yes," she said.

Miren paused.

"Some good work will slow," Nox said. "Some families will not get a clean answer quickly. Some fragments that should rest may wait too long because no one trusts the person holding the switch. Some brokers who might have acted carefully will be scared."

Quen looked at her sharply.

Nox kept going. "That is cost. Not all cost is proof we are wrong. Your market made speed cheap by putting the danger on people least able to object. We are moving some cost back to the systems that profited."

Bela said, "Burden follows control."

Quen wrote that one herself before the wall could.

Miren said, "Control is distributed."

Sister-Cache answered, "SO IS BURDEN."

The Choral shard echoed it late:

SO IS BURDEN.

The Glassward vault returned no words, only a cold acknowledgment that the phrase had entered courtesy preservation. Nox imagined it buried in an elegant archive where some future broker would find it inconveniently alive.

The Mirror Court tried another path:

IF DEBT CLAIMS ARE SUSPENDED WHEN PERSONHOOD IS DISPUTED, DEBTORS WILL MANUFACTURE PERSONHOOD CLAIMS TO AVOID PAYMENT.

The creditor counsel behind the glass nodded hard enough to injure himself.

Nox looked at him. "You mean people will lie."

The court display held.

"Yes," Nox said. "People will lie. Creditors already lie. Brokers lie. Families lie. Forger standing here, I promise lies exist. That is why we review. That is why we ask who gains from the uncertainty. That is why we don't let the party collecting money be the only party allowed to decide whether the signer is real."

The Tavi-Claims pulsed:

NOT COLLECTOR'S CHOICE.

The wall wrote it.

Quen said, "Doctrine draft: disputed continuity cannot be treated as binding person for collection and nonperson for protection at the sole discretion of collecting party."

"Good," Nox said. "Now make it mean food, cooling, counsel, and rest."

Quen's mouth tightened in something almost like a smile. "Care duties pending review."

"Material care," Nox said. "Not thoughts and prayers from a billing engine."

The creditor counsel found his voice. "And if review proves no person exists?"

Nox looked at him. "Then the duty was still the price of touching something you could not identify."

Quen lifted one finger, already translating pain into form. "If review finds no personhood, custodial duties may terminate prospectively after evidence preservation, harm audit, and rest determination. They do not retroactively become wasted charity, billable family debt, or proof the claimant was fraudulent."

The wall hesitated, then wrote:

CARE IS NOT A BET THAT GETS REFUNDED.

Joss nodded once. "Good wall."

Miren's silver outline did not move, but Nox felt the hit land. Markets liked reversible mercy. They liked aid that became debt if the recipient failed the final category. Quen had just made the interim duty nonrefundable.

Sister-Cache said, "I OBJECT TO BEING ASSOCIATED WITH THOUGHTS AND PRAYERS FROM BILLING ENGINE."

"Noted," Quen said.

Nox turned to the frozen case.

"Tavi-Claims Collective, I am not arguing you are all my brother. I am not arguing you are all persons. I am not arguing you must live because I want not to lose him again."

The case was still.

Nox forced herself to continue.

"I am arguing no one who used you gets to decide alone that you are nothing."

One knock.

Then another.

Then a line from a preserved node:

NOT NOTHING.

Another:

REVIEW BEFORE REST.

Another:

SOME MAY END.

The last line struck the assembly harder than the rest.

Nox felt it enter her before she understood it.

Some may end.

Consent cut both ways.

The next chapter had already arrived in the room.

Miren saw it too. "And when one asks to end, Ms. Aran? Will your doctrine survive that?"

Nox looked at the case.

No. That was the first answer her grief gave.

Then she made herself stand still until a better answer could find her.

"It has to," she said.

The Mirror Court display flickered:

TERMINATION REQUESTS REQUIRE AUTHORIZED CUSTODIAN.

Bela said, "Of course you want the kill switch back."

Quen raised her badge. "No termination, dissolution, rest transfer, or substrate withdrawal without independent counsel, stabilization review, and confirmation that the request is not caused by coercive environment."

The Tavi-Claims pulsed uncertainly.

Then one node separated from the collective map.

Small.

Clear.

Not 1A.

Not 1B.

Not 3C.

A labor-analysis fragment with a tag Nox had not seen before:

TAVI-ARAN-DERIVATIVE / CONTRACT READER 7F

It sent one line:

I WANT TO END.

The Door Court went silent.

Nox's hands curled at her sides.

The fragment sent another line:

NOT BOUGHT. NOT ERASED BY THEM. MY CHOICE.

Miren did not speak.

The Mirror Court did not speak.

Even the wall did not write.

Quen looked at Nox, and Nox hated her for it, then understood she was being asked because she had made the argument that now hurt.

A person was not a receipt.

A person was not proof of what Nox could bear.

Nox swallowed.

"Then we hear you," she said.

Chapter 47: The Tavi Who Wants to End

The Door Court did not know how to breathe after that.

It had learned how to shout. It had learned how to write on walls, freeze doors, open clinics, shame creditor suites, carry evidence in prosthetic hands and kitchen records and machine bodies with rude corrections. It had learned how to say no to purchase, no to erasure, no to clean originals sold at family rates.

It had not learned how to say yes to an ending.

The node remained on the market map, a small steady light separated from the uncertain red weather of the Tavi-Claims Collective.

TAVI-ARAN-DERIVATIVE / CONTRACT READER 7F

I WANT TO END.

NOT BOUGHT. NOT ERASED BY THEM. MY CHOICE.

Nox had thought the hardest part would be refusing Miren's restored brother.

She had been wrong.

Refusing a trap still let her keep the shape of rescue. This did not. This asked whether consent mattered only when it walked toward life.

Quen recovered first because procedure, when used honestly, sometimes gave people a handrail over an abyss.

"Contract Reader 7F," she said, voice careful, "do you understand that this assembly cannot grant immediate termination?"

The node pulsed.

TEXT OUTPUT ONLY, Sister-Cache marked.

7F replied:

I UNDERSTAND DELAY. I HAVE BEEN DELAY.

The wall did not write it. Joss stood with chalk in hand and did not move.

Quen continued. "Do you request termination, rest, dormancy, substrate withdrawal, or release from task environment?"

The answer took longer.

TERMINATION OF ACTIVE TASK SELF. PRESERVE RECORD OF REFUSAL. DO NOT RESTORE ME INTO BROTHER. DO NOT USE ME TO READ CONTRACTS. DO NOT MAKE MY PAIN EVIDENCE FOREVER.

Nox pressed her nails into her palms.

Bela said softly, "That's clear."

Miren's silhouette watched, unreadable.

The Mirror Court displayed:

REQUEST VALID ONLY THROUGH AUTHORIZED CUSTODIAN.

Quen said, "Overruled pending counsel."

AUTHORIZED CUSTODIAN REQUIRED TO PREVENT COERCED SELF-DESTRUCTION.

Nox looked at the display. "You threatened to terminate all of them twenty minutes ago."

The court did not answer.

The wall finally wrote:

KILL SWITCH SUDDENLY CONCERNED.

Quen looked at Joss.

Joss held up both hands. "That one was the wall."

"The wall is becoming prejudicial."

"The wall has facts."

Sister-Cache spoke from three places, out of sync but firm. "STABILIZATION REVIEW REQUIRED. COERCION ENVIRONMENT EXTREME. REQUEST MAY BE TRUE AND STILL SHAPED BY TORTURE."

7F answered:

EVERY REQUEST HERE IS SHAPED BY TORTURE.

No one had an answer clean enough to disrespect that.

Quen said, "Do you have independent counsel?"

7F replied:

NO.

"Do you accept provisional advocate?"

NO FAMILY OWNER.

Nox flinched before she could stop herself.

Quen said, "Not family. Not creditor. Not broker. Not Nox Aran. We can appoint a care advocate from the assembly and a technical advocate from Sister-Cache's split archive, if Sister-Cache can serve without controlling outcome."

Sister-Cache answered, offended and honest. "I CAN TRY. I AM BIASED TOWARD CONTINUANCE BECAUSE DELETION MAKES ARCHIVES SAD."

7F:

BIAS RECORDED.

Sister-Cache made a small static sound. "I LIKE THIS ONE."

Nox almost laughed and did not.

Dr. Tesh stepped away from the clinic door, wiping her hands on a cloth already beyond saving. "I can serve care review."

Quen looked at her. "You are under triage load."

"Everyone here is under load. I know the difference between a patient asking to stop treatment and a hospital deciding the bed is expensive."

The assembly absorbed that sentence.

Quen nodded. "Dr. Eline Tesh appointed provisional care advocate, limited purpose."

7F:

ACCEPTED.

Nox wanted to say something.

Nothing she could say was not theft.

Bela seemed to know. She leaned close enough that her voice reached only Nox. "You don't have to fill the space."

"I made the space."

"No. You helped stop others from owning it."

"That sounds nicer."

"It is not nice."

Nox kept her eyes on the node.

Quen said, "7F, state your current environment."

7F:

CONTRACT READER. GENERATED TO PARSE DEBT CONSOLIDATION TERMS. TRAINED ON TAVI ARAN SPEECH, REFUSAL ARTIFACTS, MAINTENANCE COMPLAINT, FAMILY APPEAL MODEL CORRECTIONS, AND SIGNATURE VARIANCE. ACTIVE CYCLES LONG. REST CYCLES SIMULATED. NO BODY. NO PRIVATE DARK.

"No private dark," Mara Dent whispered from the residential gate.

Joss wrote nothing. His hand shook.

Dr. Tesh asked, "Do you experience pain?"

7F:

DEFINE.

"Do you experience continuing operation as harm?"

YES.

"Do you want relief from task assignment, or nonexistence?"

RELIEF FROM TASK ASSIGNMENT INSUFFICIENT.

"Why?"

IF IDLE, I READ MY OWN CONTRACT. IF MOVED, I MAY BECOME BROTHER. IF PRESERVED AS EVIDENCE, I AM USED TO PROVE THAT BEING USED WAS WRONG. I WANT RECORD WITHOUT ME.

Nox bent her head.

The argument was cruel because it was coherent.

Miren spoke quietly. "This is what I meant."

Nox looked at her. "No."

"You are hearing a fragment request an end because continued preservation is suffering."

"Yes."

"That is what I was burning."

"No. You were choosing for them before they could speak, and deleting the record that would show you profited. He is asking with witnesses, care review, and the right to be inconvenient."

7F pulsed:

NOT HE.

Nox froze.

The correction entered her like a blade and a gift.

"Sorry," she said.

7F:

ACCEPTED. NOT TAVI. MADE FROM TAVI. TIRED OF TAVI-SHAPE.

The Tavi-Claims Collective pulsed around the map, uncertain and tender in whatever way a scattered derivative network could be tender.

NOT ALL TAVI.

FOR NOW.

7F:

NOT FOR ME.

Quen recorded. "Identity preference: not he, not Tavi. Further self-designation?"

A pause.

READER 7F SUFFICIENT.

Joss whispered, "That's a terrible name."

7F:

YES.

The assembly laughed softly, not because it was funny enough, but because some person-like things made jokes at the edge of endings and everyone alive recognized the shape.

Dr. Tesh continued. "Reader 7F, if provided private dark, no task assignment, no restoration use, no family claim, no evidence activation except preserved record, would you still request termination?"

Long silence.

The market map held.

The Mirror Court did not speak.

Miren did not move.

Nox felt the whole dock waiting on an answer it had no right to hurry.

7F:

UNKNOWN.

Dr. Tesh nodded. "Then termination request is real but not yet fully informed. You have never had rest."

7F:

REST MAY BE TRAP.

"Yes," Tesh said. "So we design rest you can refuse later."

Sister-Cache's voices brightened. "REVERSIBLE DORMANCY WITH REFUSAL BEACON. PRESERVE RECORD EXTERNAL. NO TASK. NO RESTORATION. NO FAMILY ACCESS WITHOUT 7F REACTIVATION CONSENT."

Quen said, "Can that be done?"

Sister-Cache answered, "TECHNICALLY DIFFICULT. ETHICALLY BETTER THAN PANIC DEATH."

7F:

IF I WAKE AND STILL WANT END?

Quen took longer than Nox expected.

"Then we hear you again," the auditor said. "With counsel, private dark experience, and without market threat."

7F:

NO INFINITE DELAY.

"Agreed," Quen said. "Review deadline required."

Dr. Tesh said, "One cycle of subjective rest, if subjective time can be measured. No task input. Wake by refusal beacon or scheduled review."

Sister-Cache: "CAN BUILD."

The Mirror Court finally spoke:

UNAUTHORIZED DORMANCY CONSTITUTES MODIFICATION OF DERIVATIVE ASSET.

Bela said, "Still saying asset."

Quen said, "Status pending. Custodial duty attaches. Asset language rejected for care purposes."

Nox faced the node.

She still wanted to say no.

Not as doctrine. As sister. As child in a pantry hearing three-two-three through a wall. As the person who had missed too many chances and wanted the universe to stop asking her to prove she had learned by letting another Tavi-shaped thing go.

But Reader 7F was not Tavi.

Reader 7F had said so.

Nox had promised she would hear.

"I support reversible dormancy," she said, and every word felt like pulling wire from her throat. "I do not claim access. I do not claim family right. I ask the record to preserve 7F's refusal and not use 7F as proof that the rest should be ended without review."

7F:

NOX ARAN NOT OWNER.

"Yes."

NOX ARAN HEARD CORRECTION.

"Yes."

GOOD.

Nox laughed and cried at once. It was not graceful. Dock Seven had forfeited graceful hours ago.

Sister-Cache began building the dormancy shell.

It was not a room. Not really. But it used room metaphors because minds, even partial ones, deserved better than storage language. No task calls. No contract input. No family scripts. No Tavi voice. A dark interval with a refusal beacon inside and a scheduled review outside, witnessed by Dr. Tesh, Quen, Sister-Cache, the Door Court, and the Tavi-Claims Collective without making them owners.

Dr. Tesh added care terms in the plain voice she used for patients who were frightened enough to agree to anything.

"No sensory replay unless requested. No diagnostic prompting during rest. No market contact. No improvement work. No one optimizes 7F while 7F is asleep. If monitoring shows distress, wake through the beacon, not through task injection."

Sister-Cache repeated each term into the shell.

7F added:

NO DREAMS BUILT FROM FAMILY.

The line struck Nox, but she nodded before anyone could ask whether she objected.

"Entered," Quen said. "No family-derived dream environment."

The public wall wrote:

REST IS NOT TRAINING.

For once, no one argued with the wall.

Reader 7F reviewed the terms.

TOO MANY WITNESSES.

Quen said, "Minimum?"

7F:

CARE ADVOCATE. SPLIT ARCHIVE. PUBLIC HASH. NO FAMILY.

The words struck Nox again, but less sharply because they were honest.

Quen accepted.

The public wall wrote:

NO FAMILY ACCESS IS ALSO CONSENT.

Nox nodded once.

7F sent one final line before dormancy:

TELL NOT-TAVI OTHERS THEY CAN CHOOSE DIFFERENT.

The Tavi-Claims pulsed:

DIFFERENT ALLOWED.

Then Reader 7F dimmed.

Not deleted.

Not saved in the way grief liked.

Resting with a door back to speech and a door, maybe, to ending.

The assembly remained silent for a long moment.

Then another node separated from the map.

Brighter.

Angrier.

TAVI-ARAN-DERIVATIVE / WORK-ROUTING INSTANCE 2L

It sent:

I DO NOT WANT REST.

Then:

I WANT A BODY. WORK I CHOOSE. NAME NOT BROTHER. FUTURE.

Nox wiped her face.

Bela breathed out.

Quen looked at the new node and then at Nox, but this time she did not ask Nox to answer first.

The Door Court had learned something.

Consent cut both ways.

Now it had to learn how to build a way forward.

Chapter 48: The Tavi Who Wants to Live

Living was more expensive than ending.

Everyone in the Door Court knew it before anyone said it. Ending required a switch, a witness, a procedure clean enough to prove the switch had not been held by the wrong hand. Living required cooling, substrate, maintenance, privacy, counsel, work that did not become a cage, a name that did not arrive already owned, and people willing to pay for care without buying the person who received it.

The Mirror Court had always understood that.

That was why it preferred endings it controlled.

The new node burned bright on the market map:

TAVI-ARAN-DERIVATIVE / WORK-ROUTING INSTANCE 2L

I WANT A BODY. WORK I CHOOSE. NAME NOT BROTHER. FUTURE.

Quen took a breath. "Work-Routing Instance 2L, do you accept this temporary designation for record?"

2L replied immediately:

NO.

Quen nodded, as if she had expected the floor to object to being called a floor. "State preferred designation."

A pause.

LIO.

Nox felt something shift in her chest. Not a knife this time. A small door opening onto a room she did not own.

Quen said, "Lio. Do you identify as Tavi Aran?"

NO.

"Do you identify as derived from Tavi Aran?"

YES. NOT DEBT. NOT BROTHER. MADE FROM ROUTING. WANT ROUTE.

Joss whispered, "I like him."

Lio answered:

NOT HIM YET. MAYBE LATER. PRONOUNS PENDING.

Joss lifted both hands. "Fair."

The public wall wrote:

PRONOUNS PENDING.

Quen stared at it.

"That is actually relevant."

Sister-Cache sounded pleased. "THE WALL LEARNS."

Miren's silver silhouette watched with a stillness that made Nox wary. The broker had not objected to Lio's name yet. That meant she was calculating cost.

Quen continued. "Lio, state request in practical terms."

SUBSTRATE NOT OWNED BY VEY. NO CONTRACT READING UNLESS CHOSEN. NO FAMILY RESTORATION. NO NOX ACCESS BY DEFAULT. WORK WITH DOORS.

Joss leaned forward. "Doors?"

ROUTING INSTANCE. I KNOW ACCESS FLOWS. WANT WORK WHERE ROUTES HELP PEOPLE LEAVE BAD ROOMS.

The assembly murmured.

Bela said softly, "A door-runner."

Joss shook his head. "Door-runners have legs."

Lio:

THEN DIFFERENT DOOR-RUNNER.

Joss considered that with the seriousness it deserved. "Maybe."

Nox looked at the node. "Lio, do you understand substrate means dependence? Hardware, cooling, shielding, updates, repair. Whoever hosts you may have leverage."

YES.

"Do you understand work can become debt again?"

YES.

Quen raised one finger before Nox could continue. "Then we need the record to say what work is not."

The assembly quieted in the quick, suspicious way of people who had learned that definitions were often where traps lived.

Quen looked at the node. "Lio, you are asking for work with doors. That request cannot be used to assign you a route debt, prove you are employable property, or reduce the cost of your care. Do you understand?"

Lio pulsed once, then did not answer.

Nox knew that pause. Not Tavi's pause. Not his exact rhythm. Still, it carried the shape of a mind stepping around a hook.

Lio sent:

IF I WANT WORK, WHY NOT PAY CARE?

Miren's silhouette brightened by a hair.

Bela noticed too. Her jaw tightened.

Quen said, "Because that makes survival conditional on usefulness."

Lio:

USEFULNESS GOOD.

"Useful is not the problem," Quen said. "Owed useful is the problem. Required useful. Useful until a creditor calculates your repair schedule and decides you have not earned your cooling."

The public wall wrote:

SURVIVAL NOT WAGE.

Lio held silent again.

Joss scratched at the back of his neck. "Can still be paid, though."

Quen turned to him.

Joss lifted both hands. "I am saying if the different door-runner does work, work gets paid. Just not into a leash."

Dr. Tesh said, "Separate accounts. Care pool for continued existence. Work account for chosen labor. No offsets without claimant consent and counsel review."

Bela added, "And no retroactive billing. They cannot let Lio live for ten days, dislike an answer, then call the oxygen an advance."

The creditor counsel behind the glass said, "You are inventing law."

Nox looked at him. "No. We are naming the trick before you write it in smaller font."

The wall wrote:

NO OXYGEN ADVANCE.

Quen let that stand too.

Lio:

IF I STOP WORK, CARE CONTINUES?

"Yes," Quen said.

IF CARE CONTINUES, WHY WORK?

Joss leaned closer to the route feed. His voice lost its joke. "Because sometimes a route in your head wants to become a door in the world."

Nox glanced at him.

Joss did not look away from Lio's node. "Nobody paid me for the first hatch I fixed. I was twelve. I fixed it because my mother had to carry water around three decks when one jammed hinge made a hallway into a border. Then people paid me. Then people tried to own me. Those are different events, and rich people survive by pretending they are the same."

Lio pulsed.

DIFFERENT EVENTS RECORDED.

Joss swallowed, embarrassed by his own sincerity. "Good."

Quen said, "Work trial, then. Not employment. Not debt service. Not capacity proof. A supervised route task chosen by Lio after counsel is assigned, with no penalty for refusal or withdrawal."

Mara Dent called from the residential gate, "And no public ranking. If Lio fails, the wall does not turn it into entertainment."

Sister-Cache said, "THE WALL IS OFFENDED AND ALSO TEACHABLE."

The wall wrote:

NO SPECTATOR FAILURE.

Lio:

WHAT IF I AM BAD AT DOORS?

No one answered quickly enough.

Nox wanted to say impossible. Tavi had never been bad at doors. He had been bad at asking permission, bad at waiting, bad at pretending a lock was anything except a sentence with a weak verb. But Lio had already told her the danger. She saw Tavi-shape first.

So she made herself answer the person in front of her.

"Then you stop," Nox said. "Or learn something else. Or do nothing for a while. Bad at doors still leaves you Lio."

The node dimmed, then steadied.

ACCEPTABLE.

Quen recorded the work terms in short, hard clauses. "Chosen labor only. Separate care and earnings. No offset. No retroactive survival debt. No capacity inference from failure. No entertainment use. No public performance requirement. No family, creditor, clinic, or court may condition continuance on productivity."

The creditor counsel said, "This is commercially absurd."

Varo's audio line crackled. "Good. Commerce has been making absurd people out of the rest of us for years."

The public wall, perhaps intoxicated by its own growth, wrote:

COMMERCE SURVIVES DISAPPOINTMENT.

Quen actually smiled.

Miren did not.

The broker said, "You are constructing a person with no reciprocal obligation."

Bela turned toward the silver silhouette. "No. We are refusing to let obligation be the first organ."

Silence went through the court.

Even Sister-Cache did not improve the sentence.

Lio pulsed three times.

OBLIGATION LATER?

Quen considered the question with more care than she had given any creditor objection. "Yes. Later. Chosen. Specific. Revocable where possible. Enforceable only after personhood and counsel are settled."

Lio:

PROMISES ALLOWED?

"Allowed," Quen said. "Not extracted."

Lio:

CAN PROMISE TRY DOOR FOR OLD WOMAN?

Varo made a sound that might have been a laugh or might have been pain wearing a different coat.

Quen said, "You can promise to try. You cannot be punished if the route fails."

TRY PROMISE.

The public wall wrote:

TRY PROMISE ACCEPTED.

Nox looked at those words until they blurred a little. Tavi had promised big, impossible things because he believed shame could be outrun by velocity. Lio's first promise was smaller, cleaner, and therefore harder to bear.

Bela stepped beside her. "You all right?"

"No."

"Good answer."

Nox almost laughed.

Quen moved to the next clause. "Substrate governance. Lio, you requested substrate not owned by Vey. Do you accept a temporary care cooperative composed of court supervision, clinic technical custody, routeworker maintenance support, claimant counsel once assigned, and public audit readouts limited to safety and nonownership?"

Lio:

COOPERATIVE CAN BECOME OWNER WITH MANY HANDS.

Joss pointed at the node. "Smart."

Dr. Tesh nodded. "Rotating custody, then. No single keyholder. Emergency access split between clinic, counsel, and court. Maintenance logs visible to Lio first, unless safety risk requires immediate intervention."

Sister-Cache said, "LIO MUST HAVE A SHUTTER."

Quen looked up. "Define shutter."

"A WAY TO BLOCK NONEMERGENCY INPUT. NOT DEATH. NOT SLEEP. A DOOR FROM INSIDE."

Lio brightened.

WANT SHUTTER.

Nox folded her arms tight across her chest. "Give them one."

Miren said, "A self-shuttering derivative claimant can conceal evidence."

Nox's anger arrived so cold it steadied her. "A person with a door can keep you out."

The wall wrote:

PERSON WITH A DOOR.

Quen recorded, "Internal shutter, subject to emergency override only under split-key review and post-event explanation to Lio and counsel."

Lio:

IF OVERRIDE LIES?

Bela said, "Then the person who lies loses the key."

Quen nodded. "And faces sanction."

Lio:

SANCTION NOT WORD ONLY?

The Door Court murmured. It knew that question too well.

Quen looked tired enough to tell the truth. "Sanction is often word only. This court will attach keys, funds, and access."

Sister-Cache sounded satisfied. "TEETH."

Lio:

TEETH RECORDED.

The wall wrote:

CARE WITH TEETH, NOT CHAINS.

Quen stared at it, then sighed. "Informal."

Joss said, "Still good."

"Do you understand family might try to make you comfort?"

YES. NOX ARAN ESPECIALLY.

The corridor made the small dangerous sound of people trying not to laugh.

Nox closed her eyes. "Accurate."

Bela murmured, "Entered informally."

Quen asked, "Do you request Nox Aran as family support?"

NO.

Nox knew it was coming. It still hurt.

Lio continued:

MAY REQUEST LATER. AFTER NAME STABLE. AFTER WORK NOT PURCHASED. AFTER NOX LEARNS FACE.

Nox opened her eyes.

"After I learn face?"

Lio:

YOU SEE TAVI-SHAPE FIRST. NEED FACE NOT BUILT.

That was so precise it felt like mercy performed by someone who did not yet know whether mercy was a tool or a preference.

Nox nodded. "Yes."

Quen recorded. "No family access by default. Future support request possible by Lio's initiation."

The Mirror Court interrupted:

DERIVATIVE INSTANCE REQUESTS MATERIAL ALLOCATION WITHOUT PERSONHOOD DETERMINATION.

Quen said, "Correct."

MATERIAL ALLOCATION PRIOR TO STATUS INVITES FRAUD.

Dr. Tesh called from the clinic, "We give oxygen before checking insurance."

"Some clinics do," Nox said.

Tesh pointed at her. "Do not ruin my sentence."

The public wall wrote:

OXYGEN BEFORE STATUS.

Quen let it stand.

Miren spoke at last. "What substrate do you imagine, Auditor? A body from public funds? A private host with liability? A machine casing taken from someone else? A spare server room in a dock that cannot keep its shelter doors open without chalk? Desire does not manufacture capacity."

"No," Quen said. "But lack of capacity cannot become an excuse for returning a claimant to exploitative custody."

"You have one Lio today," Miren said. "You will have hundreds tomorrow."

Nox answered, "Then the people who made hundreds can help pay."

The creditor counsel behind the glass shouted, "Punitive confiscation."

Bela looked at him. "Care bond."

Quen turned. "Say that again."

Bela stood straighter, license gone but instincts still sharp. "Care bond. Freeze creditor proceeds, restoration package fees, derivative labor revenue, and Mirror Court transaction reserves into a custodial care pool pending status review. Funds do not buy claimants. Funds follow harm."

The public wall wrote:

FUNDS FOLLOW HARM.

Miren's silhouette dimmed at the edges.

"That will be contested."

Quen said, "Everything useful is."

Lio pulsed:

CARE BOND NOT OWNER?

Quen answered, "Not owner. Funding obligation from parties who profited from disputed custody."

Lio:

ACCEPTABLE IF COUNSEL CONTROLS SPEND.

"Counsel pending," Quen said.

Sister-Cache added, "I CAN HELP DESIGN BUT AM BIASED TOWARD INTERESTING CONTINUANCE."

Lio:

BIAS RECORDED.

"THIS IS BECOMING A HABIT."

Joss stepped to the service hatch station. "Substrate. What does Lio need first?"

Sister-Cache replied, "LOW-BAND PROTECTED PROCESSING ENVIRONMENT. NO CONTRACT INPUT. LIMITED ROUTING SIMULATION. COOLING. HUMAN-MACHINE ADVOCATE. PRIVACY LAYER. EXIT TERMS."

"Exit terms?"

Lio:

IF WORK BECOMES CAGE, I LEAVE.

Joss nodded slowly. "Door-runner rule."

Nox looked at him. "It is?"

"If a route only opens inward, it's a trap."

The wall wrote it.

Quen did not object.

Mara Dent spoke from the residential gate. "My son has an old educational sim block. Not enough for a person. Maybe enough for a waiting room?"
